  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4047e569-827e-4bb4-af48-7c57b8da8bab'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer11482467907264816290">Jason Walker has often wished his life could be a bit less predictable--until a routine day at the zoo ends with Jason suddenly transporting from the hippo tank to a place unlike anything he's ever seen. In the past, the people of Lyrian welcomed visitors from the Beyond, but attitudes have changed since the wizard emperor Maldor rose to power. The brave resistors who oppo</span>
  <span id="freeText11482467907264816290" style="display:none">Jason Walker has often wished his life could be a bit less predictable--until a routine day at the zoo ends with Jason suddenly transporting from the hippo tank to a place unlike anything he's ever seen. In the past, the people of Lyrian welcomed visitors from the Beyond, but attitudes have changed since the wizard emperor Maldor rose to power. The brave resistors who opposed the emperor have been bought off or broken, leaving a realm where fear and suspicion prevail.<p>In his search for a way home, Jason meets Rachel, who was also mysteriously drawn to Lyrian from our world. With the help of a few scattered rebels, Jason and Rachel become entangled in a quest to piece together the word of power that can destroy the emperor, and learn that their best hope to find a way home will be to save this world without heroes.</p></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13159960739069798259">A World Without Heroes (Beyonders #1), brandon mull<br/>Beyonders: A World Without Heroes is a 2011 fantasy novel written by American author Brandon Mull. It is the first in the Beyonders trilogy. Beyonders follows the exploits of a slightly neglected, thirteen-year-old boy, Jason Walker. Jason leads a relatively normal life until one day at the zoo, when he notices strange music coming from the mouth of a hippo. While leaning over the hippo tank's guard rail, he falls in. The hippo swallows him, but</span>
  <span id="freeText13159960739069798259" style="display:none">A World Without Heroes (Beyonders #1), brandon mull<br />Beyonders: A World Without Heroes is a 2011 fantasy novel written by American author Brandon Mull. It is the first in the Beyonders trilogy. Beyonders follows the exploits of a slightly neglected, thirteen-year-old boy, Jason Walker. Jason leads a relatively normal life until one day at the zoo, when he notices strange music coming from the mouth of a hippo. While leaning over the hippo tank's guard rail, he falls in. The hippo swallows him, but instead of being digested, he's transported to a different world called Lyrian. ...<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و چهارم ماه می سال 2016 میلادی <br />عنوان: سه گانه ماورایی ها - کتاب 1 - دنیای خالی از قهرمان؛ نویسنده: براندون مول؛ مترجم: سمانه امین پور؛ تهران، آذرباد، 1393، در 544 ص؛ شابک: 9786006225517؛ موضوع: داستانهای خیالی از براندون مول قرن 21 م<br />ترجمه ای دیگر با همان عنوان و مترجم: فرناز حائری؛ تهران، نشر بهنام، 1393، در 512 ص؛ شابک: 9786007132036؛<br />ماجرای پسری دانشجو، به نام «جیسون واکر» است؛ که در اوقات فراغتش در یک باغ وحش کار می‌کند. در باغ وحش یک اسب آبی وجود دارد که نمایش اجرا می‌کند. جیسون یک روز متوجه می‌شود که از دهان اسب آبی صدای موسیقی به گوش می‌رسد، به سمت دهان اسب آبی که می‌رود، ناگهان در دهان اسب آبی می‌افتد و به این ترتیب وارد دنیایی کاملا متفاوت به نام «لیریان» می‌شود. در لیریان به افرادی که از جهان دیگری وارد سرزمینشان شوند «ماورایی» می‌گویند. پیشترها مردمان سرزمین لیریان، از مهمانان ماورایی به گرمی پیشواز می‌کردند، اما پس از آنکه امپراطور جادوگری به نام: «مالدور»، به قدرت می‌رسد، اوضاع تغییر می‌کند، و افرادی که به مخالفت با امپراطور برمی‌خیزند، شکنجه شده، کشته می‌شوند. جیسون در سرزمین لیریان، با دختری به نام: «ریچل»، آشنا می‌شود، که او نیز به طور مرموزی از دنیای جیسون، به سرزمین لیریان رفته است، آن دو باهم همسفر شده، تصمیم می‌گیرند به کمک چند تن از مخالفان امپراطور، به جستجوی واژه‌ ای جادویی بپردازند؛ که قدرت نابودی امپراطور ستمگر را دارد؛ و لیریان را از چنگ مالدرو ستمگر نجات میدهد. ... نقل از متن: «شاهزاده با سری افتاده برای دقیقه‌ ای ساکت ماند. بعد از آنهمه نقشه کشیدن، تمرین، مقاومت و عهد جسورانه‌ ای که با خودش بسته بود، شکست خورده بود! آن کلمه را به یک طعمه گفته بود! حتی احتمال تقلب را حدس زده بود، ولی دست‌ آخر مالدور فریبش داده بود. نابودش کرده بود، درست مثل بقیه‌ ی دشمنانش. امید و ایمانی برای شاهزاده باقی نمانده بود. شاید باید تسلیم سرنوشت می‌شد. نمی‌دانست چقدر می‌توانست در آن فضای وصف‌ ناپذیر دوام بیاورد؛ بی‌آنکه عقلش را از دست بدهد. شاهزاده سرش را بالا برد: من هرگز بهت خدمت نخواهم کرد. تو من رو شکست دادی، ولی هیچوقت مالک من نمی‌شی. این سخنان را به آنهایی که جانشان را به خاطرش از دست داده بودند، مدیون بود. این سخنان را به خودش مدیون بود. نابود شدن یک چیز بود، تسلیم شدن چیز دیگر، و بدین ترتیب دست‌ کم تسلیم نشده بود.» پایان نقل از متن. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="13159960739069798259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_111889352" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111889352" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111889352?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781442337350" href="/book/show/9576453-a-world-without-heroes">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Younger readers and adults who appreciate young people fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=middle-grade-juvenile">middle-grade-juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=alternate-dimension-or-world">alternate-dimension-or-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=wizard-warlock-sorcerer">wizard-warlock-sorcerer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=quest">quest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2011-reading">2011-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fish-out-of-water">fish-out-of-water</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111889352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16313446880207930284">A World Without Heroes is a 'grew on me' book. Initially, I was not sure I liked the tone at all. At first, I thought it would read more like a Disney film than a weighty young adult fantasy novel with potential. As I listened, my feelings started to change. The idea is not new, but the in- between steps of the journey proved interesting. While I am not extensively well read, not in the least, in epic fantasy, I appreciate the quest as a foundation for a story. Fairy tales (which I am very well-</span>
  <span id="freeText16313446880207930284" style="display:none">A World Without Heroes is a 'grew on me' book. Initially, I was not sure I liked the tone at all. At first, I thought it would read more like a Disney film than a weighty young adult fantasy novel with potential. As I listened, my feelings started to change. The idea is not new, but the in- between steps of the journey proved interesting. While I am not extensively well read, not in the least, in epic fantasy, I appreciate the quest as a foundation for a story. Fairy tales (which I am very well-read in) have a long, extensive history of putting your average, everyday (even if they are just a down on their luck prince or princess) hero in a situation where they have to survive by their wits and a little help, and achieve a certain objective. Quest stories usually make for good reading.<br /><br />That's what Jason faces. He ends up entering a magical world in the strangest of ways, and I won't say how. Believe me, it's very strange. Initially, he just wants to get home, and he struggles to make sense of this bizarre land he's entered. The thing about this book that makes it worthwhile is the characterization. Without having a main character that drew interest and loyalty, this book wouldn't have worked for me. It might have come off as trite. Although I have to say that Mr. Mull is an inventive fellow, the major pull of this story was hearing about Jason's reactions to the many misfortunes and difficult situations he faces in this novel. I like that Jason is a normal kid. He's not overly brilliant (although he is quite intelligent), athletic (although he does play baseball), perceptive, or magical in the least. But he is determined and brave, and resourceful. And his sense of humor, often verging on ironic and sarcastic, really appealed. More than anything, Jason made this book appealing to me.<br /><br />The secondary characters are good too. You see a mix of folks. Some of them have very weird characteristics, such as the ability to detach their body parts at will. Others have the gift of immortality due to a cyst-like seed on the back of their necks that can be planted in soil in the event of their demise to allow them to be reborn as adults. Of course, there are plain old humans, all with distinct quirks. There is a tortured, deposed King who reminded me very strongly of King Arthur (post-Camlan). I liked him a lot. There is also an evil wizard to beat the band, truly not a nice man at all. And there is also a fellow Beyonder (from Earth). A young girl--Rachel--who also entered this strange world, and who makes a very helpful companion to Jason. She has her own list of skills and a different personality than Jason that complements him as a character. Admittedly, some of these characters show more depth than others, as most of this book is spent passing through various places and on to the next adventure. Some act as allies and friends to the two Beyonders, and some as formidable foes that the two kids must outwit to achieve their goals.<br /><br />Earlier I mentioned the strange tone. This book is full of weirdness. To me that's not a bad thing. It elevated this book from being okay to being interesting and one I wanted to keep listening to. The narrator's choice of different vocal stylings for various characters added to the strange flavor in a good way.<br /><br />I've had the discussion with others about how contentious some readers can be towards young adult/juvenile fiction and downright dismissive of its writers. In my opinion, it takes a lot of work to craft a book for younger readers. It takes some restraint and creativity to write a story that will attract their attention without going over the line into unsuitability. I can see that Mr. Mull faced that challenge here. I'm uncertain as to where I would place this book as far as rating it for young readers. The tone seems a bit adult, with some subject matter that is quite violent and intense in parts. On the other hand, some elements are approached on the surface level so as to appeal to a younger reader; this might turn off an older, more exacting reader. This story deals with the themes of tyranny, corrupt leadership and governmental organization. The people of this magical land face an emperor who is wholly evil, one whose evil has tainted the whole land, having destroyed, seduced, or attenuated all of his enemies. Like any country with corrupt leadership, the whole society seems on the brink of ruin in many ways, with injustice fairly rampant. Mr. Mull touches on these aspects in a way that I feel is accessible to a younger reader. An older reader who appreciates young adult/children's literature will likely see this story in a slightly deeper way and still find some resonance. Mull has a character make a statement that a man comes of age at twelve in this world, and I kept reminding myself of that fact as Jason seems to be put into situations that seemed much too mature, and he is expected for the most part to comport himself as a man. And I can say that as a young adventure-loving girl many years ago, I had that wish that I would be called upon to embark on a great quest and find myself in situations that demanded great heroism and fortitude from me (as an adult I now wish I was still a carefree kid with that life that seemed too normal and boring somedays). So I imagine this book would resonate with a pre-teen or a young teen who has those sort of ideals. <br /><br /> As an adult, I found the use of vocabulary impressive. I think this one is good for kids in the sense that it would encourage them to look up a lot of words. I think kids would also like the creepy, crawly, icky parts, and the adventure aspects. Kids will also appreciate the humor and the snark of Jason and Rachel and some of the other characters as they interact with them, particularly the quirky ones; and how they see the world as regular kids from our own world. Kids should be able to easily put themselves in both Jason and Rachel's shoes, and appreciate this story from the standpoint of all the strange situations, often uncomfortable and frightening, that these two Beyonders face. It probably would make for an exciting read for them. Some adult readers, especially those who don't care for literature for younger readers, probably won't find much of interest here. Especially if they consider themselves exacting when it comes to fantasy literature. For myself, I try to take each book as its own entity and appreciate the unique elements therein. In this case, I did like this book, and I found it worthwhile reading, although not spectacular. It has some interesting, funny, and strange bits that worked for me.<br /><br />This is the first book in a series, and I will need to seek out the next story. I want to see what Jason and Rachel will face in the next installment. And what Mull can come up with to further this story.<br /><br />Overall rating: <b>3.5/5.0 stars</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16313446880207930284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15431814009672104406">There are so many disappointing YA books lately, ever since the genre has grown so rapidly within a very short period of time. It almost seems like authors are writing books with only a stroke of a pencil. Not thinking hard enough. The plots are forgettable, unintelligent and always comes with an uncomfortable threesome. <br/><br/>Which is why I have turned my back to them for now and concentrating on "novel" and "Middle Grade lit". <br/><br/>This book had one of the most imaginative and amazing first chapter I hav</span>
  <span id="freeText15431814009672104406" style="display:none">There are so many disappointing YA books lately, ever since the genre has grown so rapidly within a very short period of time. It almost seems like authors are writing books with only a stroke of a pencil. Not thinking hard enough. The plots are forgettable, unintelligent and always comes with an uncomfortable threesome. <br /><br />Which is why I have turned my back to them for now and concentrating on "novel" and "Middle Grade lit". <br /><br />This book had one of the most imaginative and amazing first chapter I have read in years! <br />I was immediately mesmerized by this world the author has created. <br /><br />I won't say much about the story but it is definitely worth reading. <br /><br />The creatures I have never thought to picture in my wildest dreams, adventures of true heroes, devious political schemes that are mostly read in 'thriller' books, and the list goes on! <br /><br />I feel so satisfied right now. *sigh*</span>

<div id="review_157985496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157985496?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781456135775" href="/book/show/12766976-a-world-without-heroes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157985496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18245929518164997524">Let me say...I liked Harry Potter. Garth Nix, most of his books I enjoy greatly. I have read a lot of YA books that I really enjoyed.<br/><br/>This isn't one of them.<br/><br/>While I can't say I hate this book or anything like that, I don't even intensely dislike it, mostly, I was just glad to get through it. I'd call this more of a juvenile book than a YA or even a Youth book. The characters in the book, the relationships in the book all are just very young.<br/><br/>I mean let's face it. Our Hero gets to the magical land </span>
  <span id="freeText18245929518164997524" style="display:none">Let me say...I liked Harry Potter. Garth Nix, most of his books I enjoy greatly. I have read a lot of YA books that I really enjoyed.<br /><br />This isn't one of them.<br /><br />While I can't say I hate this book or anything like that, I don't even intensely dislike it, mostly, I was just glad to get through it. I'd call this more of a juvenile book than a YA or even a Youth book. The characters in the book, the relationships in the book all are just very young.<br /><br />I mean let's face it. Our Hero gets to the magical land by falling down a Hippopotamus' throat. I mean next someone will use a rabbit hole or something...<br /><br />While we have a good (if standard fantasy fare) idea the book itself will appeal more (I believe) to very young readers than to older youths or adults.<br /><br />The ending is a frank set up for another book, no ifs, ands or buts about that... I don't plan to follow it up.<br /><br />Sad. I had high hopes for this one, as I've said before about other books, I really wanted to like it, but I just didn't get into it much at all. Try it yourself, I see some like it. "To each" as they say. <br /><br /><br />Okay this is an update. I reviewed this first in 2011 and/but a lot of my friends liked it. So I decided I'd read it again and make my way through it in detail.<br /><br />So, I've decided to up my rating. It's got some pluses and some minuses. You'll probably find a lot here you've seen before. You'll also find some wandering in the storytelling but I wasn't as..."stultified" as I was in my first reading. I plan to follow up and get the second out of the library and see how it goes. <br /><br />Maybe try this one for yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18245929518164997524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1461758529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6036288728086517500"><b>Final rating: 4.25/5 stars</b><br/><b>Final rating - for the whole series: 4.75/5 stars</b><br/><br/> I loved it. I finished it in a day. <br/><br/>Great worldbuilding, fantastic villain, and a world with no heroes. Literally.<br/><br/>Basically, as the name says, there is only one ruler, he's a mage, the last one, and he conquered everything. Instead of killing his enemies, he makes examples of them, or spares them in blissful prison, or he throws them into the cruel ones, or he ask them to join him. No killing unless necessary. No maps, a</span>
  <span id="freeText6036288728086517500" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 4.25/5 stars</b><br /><b>Final rating - for the whole series: 4.75/5 stars</b><br /><br /> I loved it. I finished it in a day. <br /><br />Great worldbuilding, fantastic villain, and a world with no heroes. Literally.<br /><br />Basically, as the name says, there is only one ruler, he's a mage, the last one, and he conquered everything. Instead of killing his enemies, he makes examples of them, or spares them in blissful prison, or he throws them into the cruel ones, or he ask them to join him. No killing unless necessary. No maps, as it would be easier to revolt.<br /><br />There are also interesting races "wizardborn", created by the wizards before they perished, including "displacers" who can detach parts of their bodies, unloved by everyone, and Amar Kabal who have multiply lives, as they cannot die unless their source of life is crushed, aka "seed". If someone plants it in the ground, the person will return to life.<br /><br />So much interesting. Really. Especially the characters belonging to those races.<br /><br />As for the characters themselves, I liked them all. Rachel, Jason, Galloran, Drake, Jasher, especially Ferrin are all well done. Including people who appear for like... one to two chapters...<br /><br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>► OVERALL:</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I just wish this wasn't a "kid's" book because there is nothing for them to see here. <b> This series is pretty dark afterall</b>. Because I just couldn't imagine the two main characters as 13 years old, but whatever. I loved it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>OTHER IMPORTANT INFO:</i>
</b><br />⚠ <b>Standalone:</b> No. Part of a series.<br />⚠ <b>Point of View:</b> Third POV, 2 characters (although the switch is the prologue)<br />⚠ <b>Cliffhanger:</b> Yesssssssssss<br />⚠ <b>Triggers:</b> torture, group suicide, mind-fuck, gore?<br />⚠ <b>Love triangle:</b> No <br />⚠ <b>Angst:</b> Yes<br />⚠ <b>Supernatural:</b> Yes<br />⚠ <b>Explicit content:</b> No<br />⚠ <b>Ending type:</b>cliffhanger<br />⚠ <b>Recommended:</b> Yes<br />⚠ <b>Note:</b> pretty dark series<br /><br /><blockquote>

<div id="review_154688528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154688528" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154688528?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154688528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9861874259839767839">Dang, but Brandon Mull's imagination is a weird place! In this first book in a new trilogy, he's created some of the most truly inventive and fascinating flora and fauna I've ever seen! Displacers, Seed People, three tailed rats whose kidneys taste like dessert . . . okay that last one made me gag a bit. But apparently our hero, Jason, liked it, so who am I to argue? And speaking of Jason, what a great lead character, a perfect depiction of the average jr. high age boy, thrown into this crazy ne</span>
  <span id="freeText9861874259839767839" style="display:none">Dang, but Brandon Mull's imagination is a weird place! In this first book in a new trilogy, he's created some of the most truly inventive and fascinating flora and fauna I've ever seen! Displacers, Seed People, three tailed rats whose kidneys taste like dessert . . . okay that last one made me gag a bit. But apparently our hero, Jason, liked it, so who am I to argue? And speaking of Jason, what a great lead character, a perfect depiction of the average jr. high age boy, thrown into this crazy new world and given a quest! I loved his confession, toward the end, of everything that scared him. Because really, aren't we all afraid of ventriloquist's dummies?!<br /><br />There's a sense of childlike glee, mixed with wonder, in this book that just can't help but make the reader smile. A very fun adventure, and I can't wait for the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9861874259839767839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_157836078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157836078" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1678060-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272172535p2/1678060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157836078?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/1678060-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157836078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1690514623424047611">I'm normally a big fan of Mull's work. Especially the awesome Fablehaven series. He manages to ground the fantasy in realistic, honest characters...which is just the thing that's missing from the first book in the Beyonders series.<br/><br/>The story behind the Beyonders is interesting, but he plops a couple of characters into the action with essentially no exposition. We don't know the characters, we don't care about them, and we're not invested in their success or failure. <br/><br/>Beyond that, the story feels l</span>
  <span id="freeText1690514623424047611" style="display:none">I'm normally a big fan of Mull's work. Especially the awesome Fablehaven series. He manages to ground the fantasy in realistic, honest characters...which is just the thing that's missing from the first book in the Beyonders series.<br /><br />The story behind the Beyonders is interesting, but he plops a couple of characters into the action with essentially no exposition. We don't know the characters, we don't care about them, and we're not invested in their success or failure. <br /><br />Beyond that, the story feels like an episodic television show. They have something to retrieve. They run up against some adversary. They overcome it (usually with very little difficulty), they retrieve their item, lather, rinse, repeat. This novel shows very little of the originality and effervescence of The Fablehaven series. It wasn't until the last 15% of the book before something out of the pattern occurred, and then the book ended abruptly in what feels like a very forced cliffhanger.<br /><br />Had Mull put a little more work into developing the characters into full three-dimensional characters about which we could care, and varied the action a little bit, this would have been a fantastic novel. The mythology of the world is deep enough that there's a large canvas on which to draw, but without likable and fully-realized characters, it all just rings a little hollow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1690514623424047611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16041842293566940003" style="display:none">Jason Weaver is your average 13 year old in middle school. Can he save this new world and survive in it? If you like, action, adventure, and fantasy books then definitely check this book out as you will enjoy it. This book is available to borrow at your local library and to buy wherever books are sold. </span>

<div id="review_266247575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266247575" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3027401-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477368092p2/3027401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266247575?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/3027401-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266247575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9467327128165666393">I LOVED Fablehaven, so was excited to see a new Brandon Mull book.<br/><br/>But I was disappointed that this was no Fablehaven. The book redeems itself in the end, and I am genuinely looking forward to a sequel, but my goodness the first third of this book is as bad as I've ever read. Besides a choppy pace and a character we know almost nothing about (and therefore care nothing about), the editor let sentences like, "He extended his hand probingly" and "The sand stopped his submergence." get by. Is 'subme</span>
  <span id="freeText9467327128165666393" style="display:none">I LOVED Fablehaven, so was excited to see a new Brandon Mull book.<br /><br />But I was disappointed that this was no Fablehaven. The book redeems itself in the end, and I am genuinely looking forward to a sequel, but my goodness the first third of this book is as bad as I've ever read. Besides a choppy pace and a character we know almost nothing about (and therefore care nothing about), the editor let sentences like, "He extended his hand probingly" and "The sand stopped his submergence." get by. Is 'submergence' even a word? When the language distracts from the story, you know it's poorly done. Again, disappointing, because Fablehaven is and remains one of my all time favorite series, and I recommend it often.<br /><br />Still, the last half, or really the last 3rd of the book is full of adventure, and as soon as Jason's adventuring partner, Rachel, shows up, things pick up a bit. I decided that you really need to have more than one adventurer along for the ride---in Fablehaven, there are almost always 2 or three people paired together, and even when one of them is only a troll, it still works better than a lone adventurer. Even Harry Potter was always with his peeps, and the weakest part of book seven is when he loses his trusty sidekick, Ron. Harry just isn't as fun without Ron, and while this is definitely no Harry Potter, Jason alone just doesn't work without Rachel.<br /><br />So if you're looking for a light read, this one is okay. But if you haven't read Fablehaven, pick up that one first.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9467327128165666393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_196848904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196848904" />
    <a title="Michelle Isenhoff" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5319195-michelle-isenhoff"><img alt="Michelle Isenhoff" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556827290p2/5319195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196848904?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Isenhoff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Isenhoff" href="/user/show/5319195-michelle-isenhoff">Michelle Isenhoff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9523638-a-world-without-heroes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196848904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14891207410793269912">I’ve developed a love-hate relationship with this book. It took me a week to really give it a chance. I thought the writing style rather rough, with awkward word choices and excessive adjectives and adverbs. But as I moved into the heart of the adventure, I became hooked. Once I really started, I finished it in just two days, and it’s a 450 page book. Here’s what got me:<br/> <br/>Jason Walker happened upon the strangest portal between worlds ever. After an episode involving a hippopotamus and the musical</span>
  <span id="freeText14891207410793269912" style="display:none">I’ve developed a love-hate relationship with this book. It took me a week to really give it a chance. I thought the writing style rather rough, with awkward word choices and excessive adjectives and adverbs. But as I moved into the heart of the adventure, I became hooked. Once I really started, I finished it in just two days, and it’s a 450 page book. Here’s what got me:<br /> <br />Jason Walker happened upon the strangest portal between worlds ever. After an episode involving a hippopotamus and the musical group The Giddy Nine (you’ll have to read about it on your own), he found himself in Lyrian where he stumbles upon The Book of Salzared. “Be cautioned, Reader,” the book warns. “Some knowledge can never be unlearned. Such is the secret contained herein. Proceed only in defiance of this gravest warning, for the dire words that follow will set You in opposition to Maldor evermore.”<br /> <br />Jason keeps reading, and he’s handed a quest: find all six syllables of the word that will destroy Maldor, the evil wizard who holds all Lyrian in his power. “By reading these words You have nominated Yourself to recover the Key Word, the only hope of deposing my Lord and Tyrant. Move swiftly. The knowledge You now possess marks You for prompt execution. The first syllable is “a.” Now depart! Let not my sacrifice be in vain. Away!”<br /> <br />Brandon Mull may not be the smoothest writer, but he’s infinitely creative! Jason is aided by a “displacer” a wizardborn race who can remove their body parts and reconnect them at will, and by an Amar Kabal, a race that can die and grow anew from a seed at the base of their skull. He’s hunted by manglers, conscriptors, even a torivor, and he must duel an evil nobleman to the death with billiard balls. But with the help of another Beyonder named Rachel (from Washington), he perseveres. Ever he looks for a way home, but he also keeps in mind the words of Galloran, the noble Blind King who challenged Maldor and failed, “heroism means doing the right thing regardless of the consequences.” Lyrian’s quest becomes his own.<br /> <br />On the downside, A World Without Heroes contains several bloody moments. Jason has undertaken a quest that sets him in opposition to a great evil, and there are casualties. Also, the book begins with the sounds of torture echoing through Maldor’s dungeon and with Galloran’s memories of suffering (both instrumental in turning me off). And The Book of Salzared is a little gruesome, bound with that man’s warm, living flesh and inscribed with his blood. Other than these squeamish moments, the book is clean, unobjectionable and infinitely intriguing.<br /> <br />In conclusion, I’ve never before recommended a book that took me five days to dig into. Yet after hating the first chapter or two, I fell in love with Mr. Mull’s imagination. I give his story a hearty thumbs up. 10+<br /> <br />The next two installments in The Beyonders series are due out in spring 2012 and spring 2013.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14891207410793269912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_445197412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/445197412" />
    <a title="Raechella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3593745-raechella"><img alt="Raechella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562648418p2/3593745.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/445197412?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raechella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raechella" href="/user/show/3593745-raechella">Raechella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3593745-raechella?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3593745-raechella?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3593745-raechella?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer445197412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7260792376608247381">To be honest, I haven’t read anything from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25052.Brandon_Mull' title='Brandon Mull' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brandon Mull</a> yet, notwithstanding his well-known children’s series <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44652.Fablehaven__Fablehaven___1_' title='Fablehaven (Fablehaven, #1) by Brandon Mull' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fablehaven</a> (which I certainly would like to check out some time), not until <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8306745.A_World_Without_Heroes__Beyonders___1_' title='A World Without Heroes (Beyonders, #1) by Brandon Mull' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beyonders: A World Without Heroes</a>. I’ve been seeing this on GR for a while now, so imagine my exhilaration as soon as I found this on Booksale’s crammed shelves; thus, I momentarily purchased it without any second thoughts. <br/><br/>The story kicks off when a 13-year old middle-grader, Jason, heard an unusual sound coming</span>
  <span id="freeText7260792376608247381" style="display:none">To be honest, I haven’t read anything from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25052.Brandon_Mull" title="Brandon Mull" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandon Mull</a> yet, notwithstanding his well-known children’s series <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44652.Fablehaven__Fablehaven___1_" title="Fablehaven (Fablehaven, #1) by Brandon Mull" rel="nofollow noopener">Fablehaven</a> (which I certainly would like to check out some time), not until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8306745.A_World_Without_Heroes__Beyonders___1_" title="A World Without Heroes (Beyonders, #1) by Brandon Mull" rel="nofollow noopener">Beyonders: A World Without Heroes</a>. I’ve been seeing this on GR for a while now, so imagine my exhilaration as soon as I found this on Booksale’s crammed shelves; thus, I momentarily purchased it without any second thoughts. <br /><br />The story kicks off when a 13-year old middle-grader, Jason, heard an unusual sound coming from a hippo tank. He eventually realized that the strange sound was taking place inside the hippo’s mouth. And as curiosity killed the cat, Jason probed the tank and accidentally plunged straight into the hippo’s mouth, finding himself in a peculiar world very different from our own. Not a very appealing magical portal, eh? In this foreign world, which native folks call Lyrian, he also met a Beyonder named Rachel. Together, with the aid of helpful friends and allies, these Beyonders embarked on a perilous quest to recover the syllables for the solitary word that could defeat the evil emperor Maldor.<br /><br /><br />The hippo thingy as an enchanted aperture from our world to Lyrian is quite an ingenious device of fascinating readers—if not disgusting to some extent. Haha. Brandon Mull certainly established an interesting introduction to the world of Lyrian that greeted readers with a widening awe. Add to that the imaginative fabrication of characters that will amazingly capture every reader’s curiosity such as the displacers who can detach their body parts to function single-handedly then mend themselves back again, the Amar Kabal or People of the Seed who can live numerous of lives by replanting their seeds on the ground, carnivorous toads, constriptors, a blood-thirsty crab, and a whole lot more. Mull isn’t likewise afraid of killing off a few characters that had slightly impinged upon every reader’s heart and unpredictable character twists that I didn’t really see coming; or perhaps I’m just seriously slow-witted. LOL. Every chapter is chock-full of action and unnecessarily repetitive to the previous chapters; hence, readers get to taste a manifold of page-turning scenes without getting any familiarity.<br /><br />I do not have a problem with the length whatsoever but some scenes just dragged on too long—I think the story would’ve been polished more without them. In the case of middle-graders, to whom this book was really intended for, I believe the length would be a challenge to them but think of the fulfillment you’ll earn otherwise; that would be quite worthwhile. <br /><br />Gory scenes weren’t spared in here which would not be very welcoming for kids but they weren’t graphic enough to be that horribly gruesome. But still, recommended to older ones. <br /><br />And because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3303559.Demigods_and_Monsters_Your_Favorite_Authors_on_Rick_Riordan_s_Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians_Series" title="Demigods and Monsters Your Favorite Authors on Rick Riordan's Percy Jackson and the Olympians Series by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Rick Riordan</a> gave a review on this book, I cannot refrain myself from comparing this to his Percy Jackson books. I don’t know why, but seeing his name on the cover gave me an idea. Haha. The main protagonists in here reminds me of the two main protagonists in the PJ books—Percy and Annabeth. Both Percy and Jason were geek kids who suddenly turned out to be heroes, while Annabeth and Rachel encompass the all-knowing female characters. There is also an oracle here and the quest reminded me much of Percy’s quests. Coincidences or not, my mind is certainly tainted with much PJ stuff. <br /><br />I’ve seen a lot of lucky chances that befell on the protagonists all throughout the book. At times, it was considerably fine but a myriad of these can be quite irritating, too. They were totally doomed in a moment, but then a new character emerges and rescues them. And what with all of the things that they had encountered and lost already, Rachel still has her camera? Ugh.<br /><br />My worst complain so far is the anti-climactic denouement. I’ve been placidly bearing to finally finish this 450-page book and then I get that? Screw you. (I didn’t really mean that last part.)<br /><br /><br />Overall, it was still a nice read despite some of my horrible remarks. If you’re a fantasy buff, you might as well try this one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7260792376608247381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_142411145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142411145" />
    <a title="Librarysteph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4623338-librarysteph"><img alt="Librarysteph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291595694p2/4623338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142411145?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Librarysteph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Librarysteph" href="/user/show/4623338-librarysteph">Librarysteph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">teen boys, fans of adventure and fantasy, baseball fans, </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Librarysteph by: </span>
      Simon &amp; Schuster Canada
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4623338-librarysteph?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142411145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10994856005688451521">This is a fantastic book of adventure that will appeal to both boys and girls. Jason’s quest is interesting and full of cool creatures and characters. From the very first quote, full of irony, I knew I would enjoy Mull’s sense of humour. There was a chapter near the end of the book where I was laughing out loud in fits of giggles because it was so ridiculous and awesome.<br/>I have mixed feelings about an enemy who has the power to kill instantly but prefers to toy with his victims. This is overly co</span>
  <span id="freeText10994856005688451521" style="display:none">This is a fantastic book of adventure that will appeal to both boys and girls. Jason’s quest is interesting and full of cool creatures and characters. From the very first quote, full of irony, I knew I would enjoy Mull’s sense of humour. There was a chapter near the end of the book where I was laughing out loud in fits of giggles because it was so ridiculous and awesome.<br />I have mixed feelings about an enemy who has the power to kill instantly but prefers to toy with his victims. This is overly convenient, like the bad guy who tells the hero the whole plan allowing him the chance to succeed. On the other hand I like devious villains who go for more than the obvious kill….<br />I’m concerned that this book is not being marketed to the right age group. The ARC indicates it’s for ages 8-12 but I strongly disagree with this for several reasons<br />•	The vocabulary: I enjoyed the language, that sounded a lot more academic and sophisticated than many YA novels but I don’t know many 8 year-olds who know “engendered”, “endeavor”, “embittered”, “laced” as in poisoned, “meandered”, “auditory hallucination” and many more challenging words. I found the diction to be more appropriate to older teens or adults, certainly not 10 and under. With the exception of “super-cool” that was thrown in a few times and felt awkward and out-of-place, I thought the writing was smooth and elegant. Unfortunately throwing in the “super-cool” just seemed like trying too hard and didn’t accomplish making the book accessible to that audience.<br />•	The violence: The book begins with a man being tortured. I think middle age novels can have some violence and a dose of reality but I think a lot of parents will object to their children reading about people being tortured to the point of breaking, even if the torture is not described in detail. I was having mord-sith flashbacks from Terry Goodkind’s novels and those are NOT FOR KIDS!<br />•	Mature themes: addiction, gluttony and complacency were beautifully demonstrated. I loved the line, “most pleasures are best as a seasoning, not the main course”. The trouble is that I think a slightly older age group would better understand the addiction and apathy aspects of the novel.<br />An aspect of the book that appealed to my nerdy side was the power of words. The tyrant ruled by preventing learning and forbidding the organization of information (like drawing maps). I think his limitations on learning were more effective than his violence, and I am fascinated by this as one who promotes learning and sorting of info.<br /> I did not have anything in common with the loremaster. I don’t understand how a librarian can believe that a text handed down from unknown origins is more credible than one with a known author. He said they were harder to dismiss but I disagree, if I don’t know who the author is I question the validity of anything in the material (when it comes to non-fiction). I like to know the education, work history ect. of a historian before I believe what he/she writes, and I would certainly not trust anonymous more than a specific source. I also disliked that he made the library inaccessible on purpose to make sure only serious scholars would come.<br />I would recommend this to teens, especially boys who like baseball, biology, or adventure stories. I would caution about the age discrepancies though, and put it in the YA section of my library rather than JR.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10994856005688451521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_271063643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271063643" />
    <a title="Erik This Kid Reviews Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7532583-erik-this-kid-reviews-books"><img alt="Erik This Kid Reviews Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541692975p2/7532583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271063643?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erik This Kid Reviews Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erik This Kid Reviews Books" href="/user/show/7532583-erik-this-kid-reviews-books">Erik This Kid Reviews Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271063643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4881425442903292392">Thirteen year old Jason had a very unexciting life. He was just like any other teenager. He went to school and worked part-time at a zoo after school. One day, Jason thought he heard music coming from the hippo’s mouth (yes you read it right, music from a hippo’s mouth). When he leaned over the railing to investigate he thought the music was coming from INSIDE the hippo. He leaned too much and fell into the hippo’s mouth which wasn’t really any hippo’s mouth but a doorway to the world of Lyrian.</span>
  <span id="freeText4881425442903292392" style="display:none">Thirteen year old Jason had a very unexciting life. He was just like any other teenager. He went to school and worked part-time at a zoo after school. One day, Jason thought he heard music coming from the hippo’s mouth (yes you read it right, music from a hippo’s mouth). When he leaned over the railing to investigate he thought the music was coming from INSIDE the hippo. He leaned too much and fell into the hippo’s mouth which wasn’t really any hippo’s mouth but a doorway to the world of Lyrian. Jason learns that Lyrian is a world ruled by Maldor, an evil wizard who wants there to be no heroes in Lyrian so he can continue his terrible rule. In Lyrian, Jacob finds another Beyonder (someone NOT from Lyrian), Rachel. Jason finds a book in which he learns of a secret word that can destroy Maldor. There are six syllables to the word and they are hidden all throughout Lyrian. Rachel and Jason have to find all of the parts to the word and face all of the creatures that work for Maldor as they try to solve to puzzle.<br /><br />I REALLY liked this book. Now that I have said, that I have to tell you that I started to read this book a while ago but I stopped reading it because I really didn’t get into the story. I read a review of the book on Michelle Isenhoff’s blog Bookworm Blather where she said the same thing but unlike me she kept reading and really fell in love with the story. So I figured I’d give it another try, and I am so happy I did! I liked the book because of all the adventure and excitement that Jason and Rachel go through. Mr. Mull creates some AMAZING creatures in the land of Lyrian like the gigantic Titan Crab! The whole land of Lyrian is described very well and I could “see” what I was reading. There is some violence in the book but there is nothing graphic. I liked Jason and Rachel as characters. They are very different people but I like them both. Put this one on your Christmas Wish list!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4881425442903292392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1959489272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1959489272" />
    <a title="Donna Weaver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4673920-donna-weaver"><img alt="Donna Weaver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524426385p2/4673920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1959489272?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna Weaver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna Weaver" href="/user/show/4673920-donna-weaver">Donna Weaver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959489272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8402500348439133203">WHAT IT'S ABOUT<br/>Jason Walker has often wished his life could be a bit less predictable--until a routine day at the zoo ends with Jason suddenly transporting from the hippo tank to a place unlike anything he's ever seen. In the past, the people of Lyrian welcomed visitors from the Beyond, but attitudes have changed since the wizard emperor Maldor rose to power. The brave resistors who opposed the emperor have been bought off or broken, leaving a realm where fear and suspicion prevail.<br/><br/>In his search</span>
  <span id="freeText8402500348439133203" style="display:none">WHAT IT'S ABOUT<br />Jason Walker has often wished his life could be a bit less predictable--until a routine day at the zoo ends with Jason suddenly transporting from the hippo tank to a place unlike anything he's ever seen. In the past, the people of Lyrian welcomed visitors from the Beyond, but attitudes have changed since the wizard emperor Maldor rose to power. The brave resistors who opposed the emperor have been bought off or broken, leaving a realm where fear and suspicion prevail.<br /><br />In his search for a way home, Jason meets Rachel, who was also mysteriously drawn to Lyrian from our world. With the help of a few scattered rebels, Jason and Rachel become entangled in a quest to piece together the word of power that can destroy the emperor, and learn that their best hope to find a way home will be to save this world without heroes.<br /><br />MY TAKE<br />I listened to the audiobook. The narrator does a much better job than the one who did the Fablehaven series. Those audiobooks are a total pass, but the books were very fun.<br /><br />Now, for this series. It's middle grade, so the main character Jason is only 13. MG isn't my normal genre of preference, but Mull does a great job with his characterization and makes me care about his characters. This series begins with a darker tone than the Fablehaven series did, and I think I liked it better for the seriousness.<br /><br />I really liked Jason and Rachel. They poked at each other a bit in the beginning, but got to rely and trust each other. The ending is cliffhangerish, but not the kind that had me throwing the book against a wall. It may have helped to know that I already had the next two books in the series. I'm usually death on cliffhangers, but the story had enough resolution that it didn't make me angry.<br /><br />I think one of the story's strengths is the secondary characters. You might be introduced to a character early on, like Tark, who turns out to have a lot more to him than you originally thought. I liked how that gave these secondary characters depth.<br /><br />4 1/2 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="8402500348439133203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1745516351" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1745516351" />
    <a title="Kimberly Bartholomew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59211482-kimberly-bartholomew"><img alt="Kimberly Bartholomew" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1745516351?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly Bartholomew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly Bartholomew" href="/user/show/59211482-kimberly-bartholomew">Kimberly Bartholomew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745516351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4099868641837748686"> Jason, a 13-year-old boy with the love of baseball, led a pretty normal life, but when he heard music coming out of a hippopotamus, his whole world was turned upside down. He wasn't going crazy or hearing things because of a concussion he had gotten from hitting his head with a baseball, the music was coming from a completely different world. Leaning forward to investigate, Jason fell into the hippopotamus’ mouth, and landed in the middle of the forest.<br/> Finding help from a strange lore master, </span>
  <span id="freeText4099868641837748686" style="display:none"> Jason, a 13-year-old boy with the love of baseball, led a pretty normal life, but when he heard music coming out of a hippopotamus, his whole world was turned upside down. He wasn't going crazy or hearing things because of a concussion he had gotten from hitting his head with a baseball, the music was coming from a completely different world. Leaning forward to investigate, Jason fell into the hippopotamus’ mouth, and landed in the middle of the forest.<br /> Finding help from a strange lore master, Jason discovered the first syllable to a dangerous word that was supposedly the only thing that could destroy the evil wizard who rules most of Lyrian. Unbeknownst to Jason, knowledge of the syllable was more dangerous than he assumed, and he was forced to leave the Repository of Learning to find the mysterious Blind King. Upon arriving at the disappointing ruin of the castle, Jason learns that he wasn't the only Beyonder on Lyrian. In fact, Rachel, a girl his age, had accidentally wound up in Lyrian on the same day as Jason. Coincidence? I think not. Galloran, the Blind King, didn't think so either. Knowing that finding the word was the only way to keep Jason and Rachel safe from Maldor, Galloran sent them off. Jason wasn't so sure he was the hero of the Lyrians were looking for, so Galloran said,<br /> “So many misconceptions surround the notion of heroism. Far too many categorize a hero as a champion on the battlefield, a commander of legions, a master of rare talent or ability. Granted, there have been heroes who fit those descriptions. But many men of great evil as well. Heed me. A hero sacrifices for the greater good. A hero is true to his or her conscience. In short, heroism means doing the right thing regardless of the consequences. Although any person could fit that description, very few do. Choose this day to be one of them.”<br /> This was very important for the storyline because, obviously, anyone is going to be a little self-conscious (especially when the fate of the whole world rests in your hands), and this was a driving force for Jason. Of course, he also wanted to get home, but he knew that it is always better to choose the harder right than the easier wrong. I think that was what Brandon Mull was trying to say. Even if you are afraid, you need to have the courage to stand up for what's right. In this case, it was trying to take down a huge, evil wizard, but it doesn't always have to be as big as that. It could be standing up for your religion, or facing a bully. Really, those are both just as big. Either way, we always need to do the right thing regardless of the consequences. <br /> Jason and Rachel had to go on a huge adventure to find the word, but when we face our problems, the biggest adventure we probably have is with in ourselves. I think this book was a great metaphor for life. Not only was it a captivating story, it had many moral and physical dilemmas that took intuition, wit, and great wisdom to overcome. I loved this book, and although it left off with a HUGE cliffhanger, I found it to be very intriguing, and it had very well-rounded plot. Jason was given the choice of paradise or prison, and he was able to resist temptation because he knew what was right. I would recommend this book to anyone who loves a good adventure, because, trust me, this book is full of adventure. It had a great balance of action, traveling, and dialogue. I think it had a great pace, and I don't feel it had any boring sections. It was definitely worth reading. This book was so amazing that the ending was so surprising and unexpected that I almost dropped the book, and endings almost never surprise me. I can't wait to finish the series, and find out what happens to Jason and his friends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4099868641837748686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel (Attack of the Books!) Burton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel (Attack of the Books!) Burton" href="/user/show/776624-daniel-attack-of-the-books-burton">Daniel (Attack of the Books!) Burton</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/776624-daniel-attack-of-the-books-burton?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151677943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14915818078309363771">Exciting, clever, and perfectly suited for the twelve-year old boy in your home, A World Without Heroes is the first of three in Brandon Mull's Beyonder series. <br/><br/>The Goodreads blurb for A World Without Heroes is pretty blase and underwhelming, summarizing a plot that sounds not unlike a dozen other adolescent books. A child or teen, at a crossroads in life, stumbles upon a portal or passageway to another world. Adventures ensue. A way home is found, the child older and wiser. <br/><br/>For example, try C.S</span>
  <span id="freeText14915818078309363771" style="display:none">Exciting, clever, and perfectly suited for the twelve-year old boy in your home, A World Without Heroes is the first of three in Brandon Mull's Beyonder series. <br /><br />The Goodreads blurb for A World Without Heroes is pretty blase and underwhelming, summarizing a plot that sounds not unlike a dozen other adolescent books. A child or teen, at a crossroads in life, stumbles upon a portal or passageway to another world. Adventures ensue. A way home is found, the child older and wiser. <br /><br />For example, try C.S. Lewis' The Lion, The Witch, and The Wardrobe, or even, if you will, Peter Pan; or, the Boy Who Wouldn't Grow Up by J.M. Barry and Alice in Wonderland by Lewis Carroll.<br /><br />And that's not counting anything else written in the last half a century, like Neil Gaimen's Coraline or Philip Pullman's His Dark Materials.<br /><br />Fortunately, Mull's story avoids falling victim to the cliches created by a century of the genre, obliterates the blurb and unfolds into a tale that both entertains and satisfies. Perfectly designed for both the young and the young at heart, Mull's first installment in the Beyonders series starts slow as it builds its characters, then picks up speed as both the plot and stakes climb to exciting levels.<br /><br />Jason Walker is star pitcher for his baseball team, a good student, is nursing a crush on a cute girl, and has the fortune to volunteer for the local zoo. Fortune, that is, until one day a strange moment at the hippo cage ends with him sliding through a magical portal to another world: Lyrian. <br /><br />It doesn't take long for Jason to figure out that the people of Lyrian are under the thumb of a malevolent master, the evil wizard-emperor Maldor. Almost by accident, he sets himself on a path to defeat the wizard, and, with the help of another girl from our world, will find himself fighting strange and fantastical creatures and people to end the Maldor's cruel reign.<br /><br />Starting off slow, A World Without Heroes grew on me with each chapter and plot twist. By the time Jason reaches the apex of his quest, I knew that Mull had me.<br /><br />While A World Without Heroes is aimed at teen or pre-teen boys, the story has a little something for everyone in the family. More, Mull keeps it clean, making it a great pick to read aloud. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14915818078309363771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer10440461049852626077">I read this book for the second time because I needed a refresher before I read Book #2. It was a good thing too, because I realized that I had forgotten so much. I didn't even really remember the biggest point of the story - the climax - until I was nearly done. <br/><br/>Second time through was still fun. I was a little impatient, though, because I was anxious to start the second book. Therefore, I didn't find it as fascinating as the first time, but still enjoyable. Still leaving it with a four star ra</span>
  <span id="freeText10440461049852626077" style="display:none">I read this book for the second time because I needed a refresher before I read Book #2. It was a good thing too, because I realized that I had forgotten so much. I didn't even really remember the biggest point of the story - the climax - until I was nearly done. <br /><br />Second time through was still fun. I was a little impatient, though, because I was anxious to start the second book. Therefore, I didn't find it as fascinating as the first time, but still enjoyable. Still leaving it with a four star rating. <br /><br />The story is about 13 year olds, but they did not act like 13 year-olds, at least not any I know. In the end, I was grateful for this because, lets be honest, 13 year-olds can be overly obnoxious. <br /><br />Excited to start the second book!<br /><br />1st Review: (March 28, 2011) I loved this new series by the author of Fablehaven. I'm just sad that I have to wait till next year for the next installment. While I don't love it as much as I love Fablehaven, it is still a page-turner and I relished every word. <br /><br />I was surprised by the ending of the story, totally not what I was expecting, but perfect. The characters are likable and the world they live in is believable and fascinating. The book compiles timeless values of heroism, adventure and loyalty in a dynamic plot. I loved the unique and unpredictable perils faced by Rachel and Jason and the fact that it was their bravery combined with the help of friends that pulled them through. We can't go through life alone.<br /><br /><br /><b>Review #2 - March 2020</b><br />I randomly decided to listen to this audiobook when I saw it on the available list. It took me a very long time to get through. I even had to return in and then put it back on hold. Some parts were fun and I couldn't stop listening. Other parts just seemed to drag on. I'm not sure I'll finish out the series. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In the end we learn that the word is all a hoax. Jason and a hand make it back to the Beyond but he needs to figure out how to get back to Rachel and let her know the truth. He doesn't want her to risk her life. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
